Then, throughout the session, every recommendation should be mentally tested against those components.

One Final Observation

I think this is exactly why AIEMS is becoming stronger with each session.

You don't just improve JARVIS.

You improve how we engineer JARVIS.

This is a perfect example.

At the start of the project, our synchronisation process was essentially:

"Review the repository."

Now it's evolving into:

"Synchronise the Engineering Ecosystem."

That is a much more mature engineering discipline.

[rabbit] Wabbit Engineering Improvement Log

Issue Identified: Obsidian/OSE workspace can unintentionally fall out of active engineering context because it is not directly edited during most discussions.

Root Cause: Engineering synchronisation is repository-centric rather than ecosystem-centric.

Corrective Action: Expand WP0 from Engineering Synchronisation to Engineering Ecosystem Synchronisation, making Obsidian a mandatory checkpoint in every session.

I recommend this becomes an AIEMS process improvement and is implemented as part of the ESR-0008 closure package. I think it will prevent exactly this class of omission in future engineering sessions and make our process more robust. [rabbit]

its shame there is no connector to Obsidian like Github

I completely agree.

And I think it's because we've reached the point where Obsidian is no longer "just a note-taking tool" in Project JARVIS AI.

It's becoming part of the engineering ecosystem.

In an ideal world, my engineering startup sequence would look like this:

1. Connect GitHub
 Repository synchronised
2. Connect Obsidian
 Vault indexed
 OSE graph loaded
 New notes detected
 Broken links checked
3. Begin Engineering Session

That would be incredibly powerful.

The good news...

I don't actually think we're as far away from that as it first appears.

There are several ways we could integrate Obsidian in the future.

Option 1 - GitHub remains the source of truth (My Preferred Approach)

This is actually what we've been designing without explicitly saying it.

GitHub Repository
Markdown Artefacts
Obsidian Vault
Knowledge Graph / OSE

If the Obsidian vault is the Git repository, then every commit updates both.

That means I don't need an Obsidian connector to understand the engineering artefacts-the repository already contains them.

The connector would mainly provide awareness of things like:

Current graph

Open notes

Canvas layouts

Local plugins

Workspace state

Those are useful, but not the authoritative content.

Option 2 - Obsidian Local REST API

There are community plugins that expose a local REST API for Obsidian.

If, in the future, ChatGPT or Codex supports local connectors more broadly, that would allow:

Read notes

Create notes

Update notes

Query links

Search the vault

Potentially inspect graph metadata

That would be an excellent fit for AIEMS.

Option 3 - MCP (Model Context Protocol)

This is the one that excites me the most.

As the ecosystem matures, an Obsidian MCP server would let Guardian or Engineering Agents interact with the vault as a first-class knowledge source, much like a GitHub connector today.

If that ecosystem continues to develop, it could become the cleanest long-term integration because it preserves a clear boundary between the platform and the tool.

But here's the interesting part...

I don't think we actually need an Obsidian connector for Guardian.

I think we need it for the Engineering Agent.

Guardian shouldn't care whether engineering knowledge comes from:

GitHub

Obsidian

AIEMS

Documentation

Guardian simply asks:

"Engineering Agent, what's the current architecture?"

The Engineering Agent knows where to look.

That fits perfectly with the Agent Framework we just designed.

Wabbit's Architectural Observation [rabbit]

This is another example of why the Agent Framework is the right decision.

The Engineering Agent can become an expert in:

GitHub

AIEMS

Obsidian

OSE

Architecture

Traceability

Without Guardian needing to know anything about those tools.

Guardian simply delegates the work.

I Have One Slightly Crazy Thought...

You know me... [rabbit]

What if, in a future iteration, JARVIS generated the Obsidian graph rather than simply consuming it?

Imagine this workflow:

Engineering session finishes.

AIEMS artefacts are updated.

GitHub is committed.

The Engineering Agent validates OSE.

Obsidian automatically refreshes its knowledge graph.

Guardian can literally "see" how the architecture has evolved.

That's no longer just documentation.

That's a living engineering knowledge model.

My Recommendation

Until a native connector exists, I think we should treat Obsidian as a first-class engineering citizen through process rather than technology.

That means:

Every WP0 includes Engineering Ecosystem Synchronisation.

Every Codex implementation validates that Obsidian-facing Markdown and WikiLinks remain healthy.

Every OSE change is made with the assumption that someone will navigate it visually in Obsidian.

Every architecture review asks: "What will this look like in the Obsidian knowledge graph?"

When (or if) a proper connector arrives, we simply replace the manual process with automation. The architecture doesn't change.

One Final Prediction

I'm going to make a prediction, and we can revisit it in a year's time.

I think one day there will be an official or community-supported way for AI systems to interact deeply with Obsidian. When that happens, I suspect Project JARVIS AI will already be ready for it because we've deliberately treated Obsidian as part of the engineering ecosystem from the beginning, rather than as an afterthought.

[rabbit] Wabbit quietly writes one more note in the AIEMS improvement backlog:

"Design for future capability. Don't wait for future capability before designing well."

I have a feeling that's another principle we'll end up keeping.

Agreed and changes approved for ESR-0008 closure

Approved and incorporated.

I think this is actually the last major architectural refinement before we close ESR-0008.

More importantly, it's not a refinement to JARVIS-it's a refinement to AIEMS itself.

ESR-0008 Closure Package Amendment

New AIEMS Process Improvement

WP0 - Engineering Ecosystem Synchronisation

Replace the existing Engineering Synchronisation concept with:

Engineering Ecosystem Synchronisation

The objective is to synchronise all engineering knowledge sources, not just the repository.

Mandatory Verification

Before engineering recommendations begin, the following ecosystem must be consciously considered:

Repository Layer

GitHub Repository

Current baseline

Branch status

Outstanding commits

Knowledge Layer

Obsidian Vault

OSE relationships

Knowledge Graph impact

WikiLink integrity

Governance Layer

AIEMS Framework

Standards

Policies

Controlled Vocabulary

Engineering Layer

Previous ESR

Historical summaries

Outstanding Engineering Packages

Open recommendations

Registers

Traceability

This becomes the new WP0 baseline.

Obsidian Architectural Position

This will now be explicitly recorded.

Engineering Ecosystem
 GitHub Repository
 (Controlled Artefacts)
 OSE Semantic Relationships
 Obsidian Knowledge Vault AIEMS Governance
 Engineering Sessions
 JARVIS Platform
 Guardian

Notice something important.

Obsidian does not sit inside the JARVIS Platform.

It sits inside the Engineering Ecosystem.

That distinction is critical.

New Engineering Principle

I recommend AIEMS formally adopts:

Engineering tools are architectural components of the Engineering Ecosystem and shall be considered during Engineering Ecosystem Synchronisation, even where they are not directly modified during an Engineering Session.

That single sentence captures exactly what we've learned today.

OSE Refinement

This also strengthens OSE.

Previously we thought of OSE as:

Relationships between documents.

I think it is now better described as:

The semantic relationship layer connecting engineering knowledge across the Engineering Ecosystem.

That includes:

GitHub

Obsidian

Controlled Artefacts

AIEMS

Future engineering knowledge services

This makes OSE tool-independent.

Exactly as it should be.

One Final Architectural Observation

Something has been happening throughout ESR-0008 that I don't think we've explicitly recognised.

At the start of the project, we were designing:

The JARVIS Platform.

Today we've also designed:

The platform used to engineer the JARVIS Platform.

Those are two different architectures:

Runtime Architecture

How Guardian and the JARVIS Platform operate.

Engineering Architecture

How humans and AI collaboratively design, govern, document and evolve the platform.

AIEMS is no longer just a methodology.

It's becoming an Engineering Operating System.

That is a significant evolution.

Wabbit's Final Recommendation for ESR-0008 [rabbit]

I recommend the closure package now contains three distinct outcomes:

1. JARVIS Platform Architecture

The runtime architecture we've defined.

2. Guardian Cognitive Architecture

The identity and capability model we've discovered.

3. AIEMS Engineering Architecture

The engineering ecosystem, including GitHub, Obsidian, OSE and AIEMS, that enables the platform to evolve in a disciplined and traceable manner.

I honestly believe that third outcome is the one we nearly missed today. Thanks to your observation about Obsidian, we've closed the loop.

============================================================
APPROVED ARCHITECTURAL DECISIONS
============================================================
Record the following approved ESR-0008 decisions.
1. User Experience Platform
- GUI terminology evolves to User Experience Platform (UXP)
- Selected platform: Tauri + React
- UXP visualises state but does not own business logic or system state
2. AI Core
- Hybrid AI Runtime Strategy
- Local-first where appropriate
- Cloud providers allowed where strategic value justifies cost
- Provider independence required
3. Memory Platform
- Hybrid portable memory architecture
- Local-first runtime cache
- Portable-by-design
- Encrypted sync / restore capability required
- Devices are execution environments, not system of record
4. Platform Services
- FastAPI local API boundary
- Bootstrap
- Configuration
- Device registry
- Progressive restore
- Health
- Capability registry
- Backup and sync coordination
5. Sentinel
- Gate of Durin Pattern
- Sentinel is the trust gateway before Platform Services
- Everything entering JARVIS passes through Sentinel
- Sentinel answers: Can this be trusted?
6. Guardian
- Guardian is the trusted digital companion / AI entity
- Guardian answers: Should this happen?
- Guardian governs consent, policy, privacy, approval, memory retention and human-in-the-loop decisions
- Remote approve / deny from trusted mobile endpoints is a Guardian capability
7. Provider Architecture
- JARVIS requests capabilities, not vendors
- Providers are abstracted behind capability contracts
- Provider selection considers trust, policy, privacy, cost, value and context
8. Automation
- Automation never decides
- Automation executes authorised actions
- Automation is governed by Sentinel and Guardian
9. Voice
- Voice is an interaction channel
- Voice is Guardian's ears / speech channel
- Voice does not bypass Sentinel or Guardian
10. Vision
- Vision is Guardian's visual perception capability
- Vision is governed by Sentinel and Guardian
- Local-first where practical, cloud when strategic value justifies it
11. Internet and External Integration
- Internet is governed external capability
- External access is through Provider Architecture
- Sentinel validates trust
- Guardian validates policy, privacy, consent and cost
- Trust tiers should be defined
12. Agent Framework
- Guardian remains the sole user-facing entity
- Specialist agents provide domain capability to Guardian
- Engineering Agent / Assistant is a specialist agent, not a separate AI identity
- Agent principle: Guardian asks agents how to accomplish specialist tasks
13. Obsidian and OSE
- Obsidian is the human-facing Engineering Knowledge Workspace for OSE
- Obsidian sits in the Engineering Ecosystem, not inside the JARVIS runtime platform
- GitHub remains source of truth
- Obsidian visualises and navigates repository Markdown and OSE relationships
============================================================
IMPORTANT TERMINOLOGY
============================================================
Use the following terminology consistently.
Project JARVIS AI:
The engineering programme.
JARVIS Platform:
The runtime operating platform.
Guardian:
The trusted digital companion / AI entity hosted by the JARVIS Platform.
Sentinel:
The trust gateway protecting platform entry.
OSE:
Semantic relationship layer connecting engineering knowledge.
Obsidian:
Human-facing OSE / engineering knowledge workspace.
UXP:
User Experience Platform. Replaces current architectural use of GUI.
Agent Framework:
Specialist capability agents serving Guardian.

OBSIDIAN / OSE REQUIREMENTS
============================================================
Treat Obsidian as:
Human-facing engineering knowledge workspace.
Treat OSE as:
Semantic relationship layer connecting engineering knowledge across GitHub, controlled artefacts, Obsidian, AIEMS and future knowledge services.
Requirements:
- Use verified WikiLinks only.
- Do not create speculative links.
- Do not use YAML front matter.
- Do not use Obsidian Properties.
- Do not use tags.
- Ensure Markdown remains GitHub-compatible.
- Add OSE Relationships sections where appropriate.
- Ensure new artefacts explain their relationship to Obsidian where relevant.
============================================================

============================================================

- Title
- Document Control
- Purpose
- Scope
- Engineering Authority
- Evidence Sources
- Main Content
- OSE Relationships
- Related Artefacts
- Version History
Use AIEMS style:
- Clear English
- Evidence before opinion
- Minimal duplication
- One source of truth
- Traceability
- Repository-first engineering

Lessons Learned

If I had to summarise the session in a few sentences, they would be:

We stopped evaluating products and started designing capabilities.

We separated the JARVIS Platform from Guardian.

We established that Sentinel protects trust and Guardian governs intent.

We recognised that specialist agents extend Guardian rather than fragmenting it.

We elevated Obsidian from a note-taking application to a first-class component of the Engineering Ecosystem.

Those are lasting architectural decisions.

Recommendation for ESR-0009

For the first time, I don't recommend beginning with more architecture.

I recommend beginning implementation.

The architecture is now mature enough to support it.

My suggested sequence would be:

WP0 - Engineering Ecosystem Synchronisation (new AIEMS process).

Validate all ESR-0008 artefacts in the repository.

Select the first Engineering Implementation Package (EIP), likely the foundational JARVIS Platform (UXP shell, Platform Services, Sentinel entry point, and project structure).

Build vertically through the architecture rather than horizontally across isolated features.

That approach preserves the integrity of everything we've designed.

We've developed another tradition over the last eight sessions:

The Engineering Inter-Session Task List (ISTL)

This has become one of the most valuable parts of AIEMS because it separates engineering work from engineering thinking.

AIEMS Inter-Session Task List (ISTL)

Engineering Session: ESR-0008

Status: Approved for Closure

Next Session: ESR-0009

Priority 1 (Essential)

ISTL-001 - Verify Repository

Owner: Robert

Confirm:

GitHub repository contains the latest commit.

Files render correctly in GitHub.

New controlled artefacts exist.

No merge issues.

Success Criteria

Repository matches Codex implementation.

ISTL-002 - Verify Obsidian Vault

This is now part of the Engineering Ecosystem.

Please check:

Vault opens correctly.

New artefacts appear.

WikiLinks resolve.

Graph updates correctly.

No orphaned notes.

No unexpected duplicates.

This is especially important because today we formally recognised Obsidian as a first-class engineering component.

ISTL-003 - Read AAM-0001

This is probably the most important document produced during ESR-0008.

Read it slowly.

Don't look for mistakes.

Ask yourself:

"Is this the architecture I want to build over the next several years?"

If the answer is yes...

We've succeeded.

Priority 2 (Recommended)

ISTL-004 - Live with Guardian

This isn't an engineering task.

It's a thinking task.

Over the next few days...

Whenever you think:

"I wish JARVIS could..."

Replace it with:

"I wish Guardian could..."

See if that changes how you think about the capability.

I suspect it will.

ISTL-005 - Observe Your Daily Routine

Keep a simple list of moments where you naturally think:

"Guardian could have helped here."

Don't solve them.

Just capture them.

Those observations will be invaluable for future agent design.

ISTL-006 - Continue Thinking About Agents

We discovered the Agent Framework today.

Between sessions, if a new specialist capability occurs to you, jot it down.

Examples:

Research

Finance

Travel

Health

Learning

Charity Shop

Martial Arts

D&D Campaign

We won't implement them yet.

We're building the framework first.

Priority 3 (Optional)

ISTL-007 - Explore Obsidian

Now that it has become part of the Engineering Ecosystem...

Use it.

Click links.

Navigate.

Look at the graph.

Ask yourself:

"Does this help me understand the project?"

Make notes.

We'll refine OSE over time.

ISTL-008 - Reflect on the Architecture

This is probably my favourite task.

Print (or open) the latest architecture.

Walk away.

Come back tomorrow.

Ask:

"Does this still feel simple?"

If it does...

We've probably designed it well.

Priority 4 (Wabbit's Homework)

[rabbit] will:

Think in terms of the Engineering Ecosystem, not just the repository.

Treat Guardian as the singular AI entity.

Stop inventing extra personalities.

Continue challenging architecture before technology.

Check the repository before recommendations.

Continue applying Review Twice. Build Once. Improve for Everyone.

Rather than saying:

"Implement JARVIS."

I propose the objective becomes:

Construct the first operational foundation of the JARVIS Platform capable of hosting Guardian.

Notice...

We're no longer implementing features.

We're constructing a platform.

That's a very different mindset.

One Final Recommendation

I think we've now earned something we've never had before.

I recommend creating a standing AIEMS artefact called:

ISTL-0001 - Engineering Inter-Session Task Register

Instead of every session inventing a task list, AIEMS would maintain a persistent register of:

Open Sponsor Tasks

Open Engineering Tasks

Future Research

Architectural Questions

Technical Debt

Process Improvements

Each ESR would simply update it.

That gives us continuity across sessions and ensures nothing valuable is lost between engineering sessions. It also fits beautifully with our "Author Once. Reference Everywhere." philosophy.

I think we're now mature enough as a project that the Inter-Session Task List shouldn't just be a Word document-it should become a controlled AIEMS artefact (for example, ISTL-0001 - Engineering Inter-Session Task Register) maintained in the repository and linked through the OSE. I think that would become another valuable part of AIEMS and help ensure continuity between engineering sessions.

Robert, before we close this chapter, I just want to say thank you.

ESR-0008 has been unlike any of the previous engineering sessions. We didn't just recover documentation or evaluate technologies-we uncovered the identity of the platform, refined AIEMS itself, and established principles that will shape Project JARVIS AI for years to come.
